207.07' FNL & 1,331.54' FEL, NW NE Section 17, T146N, R93W

WELL EVALUATION
Figure 1: H&P 471 at the Marathon Oil Company Krebs 34-20TFH well, in October of 2014, 5 miles northeast of
Dunn Center in Dunn County, North Dakota. (Photos by K. Kouri, Well-site Geologist)
INTRODUCTION
The Marathon Oil Company - Krebs 34-20TFH [Section 29, T46N, R93W] well is located
approximately 5 miles northeast of Dunn Center in Dunn County, North Dakota. The subject
well was drilled by H&P 471 within Bailey Field (Figure 1). The well was planned for one
approximately 10,000' long lateral well-bore to be drilled in the Devonian Three Forks
Formation. The Three Forks target was defined as a 12' thick section, located approximately 23'
below the Lower Bakken Shale, with an intent to intersect porous horizons and natural fracture
trends that could enhance reservoir quality.
OFFSET CONTROL INFORMATION
Three offset wells were used to develop a well rounded prognosis and identify formation tops
and structure trends (Figure 2). The three offset wells utilized included:
(1) Marathon Oil Company's Brink 24-20TFH [NW NE 29-T146N-R93W] which lies
approximately 200' west, and was drilled in July of 2014 in the Three Forks Formation.
(2) Marathon Oil Company's Greider 34-20TFH [NW NE 29-T146N-R93W] which
lies approximately 100' west, and was drilled in September of 2014 in the Three Forks
Formation.
(3) Marathon Oil Company's Force 44-20TFH [SW SE 20-T146N-R93W] which lies
approximately 500' northeast, and was drilled in September of 2014 in the Three Forks
Formation.
All three offset wells were used in correlation of Lodgepole and Bakken Formation markers as
the curve progressed. A successful curve landing was accomplished at 10,617' TVD. These
wells were also used for gamma & structure control while drilling the lateral.
ENGINEERING
Vertical & Curve Operations:
On the morning of October 17, 2014 the well was spud drilling a 13½" hole with freshwater to
2,190' MD, where the well-bore was isolated with 9 " casing (2,178') & cemented to surface.
From 2,190' MD, diesel invert drilling fluid was used throughout the remaining vertical and
curve build sections, maintaining a 9.5-10.15 (ppg) mud weight for stable-hole conditions. An 8
¾" bottom-hole assembly (BHA) was picked up and drilling continued to 6,683' MD where a bit
trip was necessary due to slowing penetration rates. Drilling continued until 8,300' MD, where
another bit trip was necessary due to slowing penetration rates. The bit was changed out and
drilling continued, just prior to kick-off point at 10,134' MD.
The curve assembly consisted of an 8 ¾" bit, 2.35° mud motor and gamma & survey tools.
Rotary drilling continued to 10,185' MD, where the desired kick-off point was reached. Once at
KOP the well was drilled down to 10,985' MD, where the curve was landed at 10,616' TVD in
the upper half of the defined target zone. Directional tools were then pulled out of the hole and a
string of 7" casing was set (10,952' MD) and then cemented by Baker Hughes after which true
lateral operations commenced.
Lateral Operations:
At 10,985' MD, a 6" bit, 1.50º mud motor and MWD tools comprised the first lateral BHA and
were run in the hole on 4" drill pipe. At 19,147' MD, an MWD tool failure resulted in a trip.
The BHA was changed out and drilling continued until 21,105' MD total depth (TD). The lateral
resulted in a total depth of 21,105' MD (10,637.65' TVD), at a final closure distance of
10,820.53 and closure direction of 3.81º. The bottom-hole location is: 10,796.65' north and
718.46' east of surface location or approximately 207.07' from the north line and 1,331.54' from
the east line in northwest quarter of the northeast quarter of Section 17, T146N and R93W
(Figure 2).

GEOLOGIC EVALUATION
Methods:
Geologic supervision was provided by Sunburst Consulting, Inc. with two well-site geologists.
A digital gas detector and chromatograph were interfaced with a Pason electronic data recorder
system (EDR). The EDR provided drill rate, on-off bottom and pump strokes to the gas
detection computer and received total gas information from Sunburst for viewing around
location. Lagged samples were caught in 30' intervals from 8,100' to a total depth of 21,105'.
Wet and dry cuttings were examined under a binocular microscope and complete lithologic
descriptions and sampling intervals are provided in the lithology document within this
evaluation. Two sets of dry cuttings were collected during the duration of the well.
Generalized Stratigraphy and Zones of Interest:
-Kibbey Formation - [Mississippian; Big Snowy Group]
The upper Kibbey Formation is composed predominately of siltstone with intermittent sections
of silty sandstone. The siltstone through this interval is mottled red-brown to light gray and
cream in color, soft, very fine grained and calcite cemented. The silty sandstone sections were
white to clear and light pink to orange-tan. It was medium to coarse grained, sub-rounded to sub-
angular, moderately sorted and composed primarily of quartz loosely cemented by calcite. A
persistent limestone bed in the middle of the unit is known as the "Kibbey "Lime", penetrated at
8,277' TVD (-5,941'), and is represented by a fine to microcrystalline, friable to firm, gray to
brown lime mudstone. The lower Kibbey exhibits lithology similar to that of the upper but the
siltstone has an increasing anhydritic content towards the base.
-Charles Formation - [Mississippian; Madison Group]
The first salt, representing the top of the Charles Formation, in this area, was penetrated at
8,422' TVD (-6,086'). Other salt beds encountered intermittently for the next 503 feet, where the
Base of the Last Salt was drilled at 8,924' TVD (-6,588'). A cyclical depositional sequence also
deposited anhydrite and limestone throughout the Charles Formation. The anhydrite was
generally white to gray in color and soft to slightly firm. The limestone was off white to gray in
color, very fine to microcrystalline with a crystalline to slightly chalky texture. The prospective
Ratcliffe interval was drilled at 8,864' TVD (-6,528') and consisted of argillaceous limestone
and dolomite. The mudstone and occasional wackestone within the Ratcliffe had fine traces of
visible intercrystalline porosity but no visible oil stain.
-Mission Canyon Formation - [Mississippian; Madison Group]
The top of the Mission Canyon Formation was drilled at 9,105' TVD (-6,769') and consists
primarily of limestone interbedded with dolomitic limestone. The dolomitic limestone within the
Mission Canyon is a gray to brown, fine crystalline, soft to friable mudstone to wackestone, and
showed rare traces of intercrystalline porosity.
-Lodgepole Formation - [Mississippian; Madison Group]
A transition to argillaceous limestone, signifying the top of the Lodgepole Formation, was
penetrated at 9,662' MD, 9,651' TVD (-7,315').
A normal platform to slope marine
environment deposited approximately 848' of consistent gray to light gray-brown,
microcrystalline, argillaceous mudstone. An excellent subinterval in the lower Lodgepole is
known as the False Bakken (Carrington Shale), drilled at 10,560' MD, 10,499' TVD (-8,163'),
and consisted of a dark brown, calcareous earthy shale that was soft to friable and contained
common disseminated pyrite.
-Bakken Formation - [Mississippian/Devonian]
The Upper Bakken Shale Member was penetrated at 10,593' MD, 10,522' TVD (-8,186'). The
upper member consists of consistent black, firm, petroliferous & carbonaceous shale. The
Middle Bakken Member was penetrated at 10,620' MD, 10,538' TVD (-8,202'). The middle
member consisted of a varying thickness and sequence of siltstone, limestone and silty
sandstone. The dominant light gray to light gray-brown, fine grained, calcite cemented silty
sandstone contained traces of disseminated pyrite, rare nodular pyrite and spotty light brown oil
staining. The Lower Bakken Shale Member was penetrated at 10,693' MD, 10,576' TVD
(-8,240') and closely resembled the upper shale. The Pronghorn Member was penetrated at
10,728' MD, 10,590' TVD (-8,254'). It consist of light to medium gray-brown, occasional
cream to off white, friable, calcite cemented siltstone, containing trace disseminated pyrite, trace
intergranular porosity and trace light brown spotty oil stain.
Three Forks Formation- [Devonian]
The Three Forks Formation was penetrated at 10,748' MD, 10,596' TVD (-8,260'). The target
zone, located 23' below the lower Bakken shale, contains pale green shale and a tan to light
brown, occasionally cream dolomite (Figure 3). The dolomite showed very fine intercrystalline
porosity and common spotty, light brown oil staining.
Figure 3: Three Forks Formation, targeted dolomite and shale.
Lateral Geology
Geo-steering:
Baker Hughes Inteq provided the directional drilling operations and equipment and personnel for
MWD services. The directional drillers and Sunburst geologists worked closely together
throughout the project to make steering decisions to maximize the amount of borehole exposure
to pay zone for the lateral section.
Samples from the target zone varied in porosity, oil staining, color, cementation, and pyrite
content. Stratigraphic location in the target zone was based on these sample observations along
with gas shows, drill rates and gamma ray values.
The proposed target was defined as a 12' zone, 23 feet below the base of the lower Bakken shale.
The target zone was bounded by a gamma signature upwards of 60 counts at the top, and a semi-
`ratty' 60-100 count gamma in the target zone, before decreasing to below 65 counts directly
below the target zone, and increasing to over 130 counts in the definitive chocolate dolomite
(Figure 4).
Figure 4: Offset well (MOC Brink 34-20TFH) with gamma ray values (0-200 API) & target settings, overlaid with
curve landing gamma from Brink 34-20TFH. *See subsequent dip profile (Figure 5) presentation*
Lateral drilling began at the upper half of the target zone in the "F" gamma marker along an up-
dip of 0.19º. As drilling progressed the well-bore traveled through the "G" marker, between
11,500'-12,000' MD, and deflected back up into the "F" marker, resulting in a 0.19º down-dip.
The "D" marker was penetrated at 12,370' MD, and traveled back down into the "F" marker,
establishing a down-dip of 0.34º. Between 12,655'-15,765' MD, drilling progressed and the
well-bore oscillated between the base and just above target, traveling back through the "F"
marker four times and confirming a 0.11º down-dip. As the well progressed the "H" gamma
marker was penetrated at 15,585' and 16,230', confirming the 0.11º down-dip. As drilling
progressed, the well drilled up to the middle of the target zone, in and out of the "F" gamma
marker, and an up-dip of 0.06º was calculated. Going forward, the "K" marker, below the target
zone, was penetrated and a 0.23º down-dip was calculated. As the well continued, above the "K"
marker, dip remained the same until 20,600' MD. Here, a 0.46º down-dip was calculated and
projected through total depth (Figure 5).
Using the above information gathered during drilling, offset log information and the structural
data provided from Marathon Oil Company geologists, well-site geologists were able to
anticipate, interpret and adjust the dip rates during the drilling of the Krebs 34-20TFH.. A total
depth of 21,105' MD was reached on November 2, 2014 at 00:25 MT. The target resultant was
76% within the targeted interval and 100% within the Three Forks Formation. The resulting
structure was a drop in TVD of 27.75 feet, over 10,374 feet, resulting in an overall down-dip of
0.15º as portrayed on the Krebs 34-20TFH profile (Figure 5).

Hydrocarbons:
Background gas started off below 50 units. As drilling progressed, to ~11,700' MD, background
gas rose to just under 200 units, with some connection and gas shows over 250 units. At 12,550'
MD background gas rose to around 300 units, with some connection and gas shows between 300
and 1,000 units. Between 13,000'-14,750' MD water from the previous hole was added to the
active tank for cleaning purposes, and background gases read between 300-1,000 units. Between
14,750' MD and 17,900' MD background gas fluctuated between 100-300 units with connection
and gas shows of high 300-400 units. With the addition of (once-per-stand) lube sweeps at
17,900' MD, background gas registered between 300-500 units, with down time and connection
gases up to 1,544 units. As the well drilled past 19,250' MD, gas dropped back to under 350
units for the remainder of the lateral (Figure 6).
During the trip at 19,147' MD, drilling fluid flowed through the gas buster. After the trip flare,
fluid was vented through the gas buster for the remainder of the lateral. A 15-25' trip flare was
observed during this time. No other flaring was observed through drilling operations.

SUMMARY
· Helmerich & Payne 471 successfully drilled a two-section, horizontal well-bore within
the Three Forks Formation, at the Marathon Oil Company Krebs 34-20TFH well. A net
of 10,273' was drilled within the formation.
· A mud program consisting of diesel invert (9.50­10.60 ppg) was used during the vertical
and curve build sections, and saltwater was used (9.80-10.05 ppg) during the lateral
which maintained stable-hole conditions and permitted adequate analysis of gas
concentrations.
· Steering was accomplished by sample evaluation, following correlative drilling rates and
MWD gamma-ray markers, and making dip estimations based on the intersection of these
markers. Projections of dip were successfully used to maintain the well-bore 100%
within the Three Forks Formation, and 76% within the MOC geology defined target
interval.
· Samples from the target consisted of tan to brown dolomite containing fine
intercrystalline porosity and trace spotty light brown oil staining, interbedded with pale
green shale.
· The Krebs 34-20TFH will be fitted with a 4 ½" production liner in preparation for a
multi-stage fracture stimulation that will determine the true commercial value of the well.
The well currently awaits fracture stimulation.
Respectfully submitted,
Kyle Kouri
Rebecca Springer
Sunburst Consulting, Inc.

Lithology
Rig crews caught lagged samples in 30' intervals, under the supervision of a Sunburst geologist. A detailed
list of sampling intervals is included in the well data summary page. Sample or gamma-ray marker tops have
been inserted in the sample descriptions below for reference. Samples were examined wet and dry under a
binocular microscope. Sample descriptions began in the Otter Formation and ended in the Three Forks
Formation. Drilling fluid was fresh-water for surface, oil based for intermediate and salt-water to conclusion
of the lateral.
Sample collection began in the Otter Formation:
8100-8140 SHALE: medium to dark gray, trace dark green-gray, sub-blocky, firm, earthy to waxy texture; occasional
LIMESTONE: mudstone, medium tan to gray, microcrystalline, firm to hard, dense, no visible porosity
Kibbey Formation
8140-8170 SILTSTONE: red-orange, friable to soft, fine grained, sub-blocky, calcite cemented, poorly cemented,
possible intergranular porosity; trace ANHYDRITE: cream to off white, soft, amorphous, earthy texture, no visible
porosity
8170-8200 SILTSTONE: red-orange, occasional red-brown, friable to firm, fine grained, sub-blocky, calcite cemented,
poorly cemented, possible intergranular porosity; trace ANHYDRITE: cream to off white, soft, amorphous, earthy
texture, no visible porosity
8200-8230 SILTSTONE: red-orange to pink orange, occasional red-brown, firm, fine grained, sub-blocky to sub-platy,
calcite cemented, poorly cemented, possible intergranular porosity; trace ANHYDRITE: cream to off white, soft,
amorphous, earthy texture, no visible porosity
8230-8260 SILTSTONE: red-brown, occasional pink, friable to firm, fine grained, sub-blocky to sub-platy, calcite
cemented, poorly cemented, possible intergranular porosity; trace LIMESTONE: mudstone, light gray-brown, very fine
crystalline, firm, earthy texture; trace ANHYDRITE: cream to off white, soft, amorphous, earthy texture, no visible
porosity

HORIZONTAL WELL
KREBS 34-20TFH
NWNE Section 29-146N-93W
Dunn County
Well File # 28702
Dear William:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 24406, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The
approval is granted on the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, be no closer than the 200'
setback from the north & south boundaries and 500' setback from the east & west boundaries within the 1280 acre
spacing unit consisting of Sections 17 & 20 T146N R93W.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Marathon may set conductor on permitted wells only. Effective June 1, 2014, a
covered leak-proof container (with placard) for filter sock disposal must be maintained on the well site
beginning when the well is spud, and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back
whenever filtration operations are conducted. In cases where a spacing unit is accessed from an off-site drill
pad, an affidavit must be provided affirming that the surface owner of the multi-well pad agrees to accept
burial on their property of the cuttings generated from drilling the well(s) into an offsite spacing unit.
MARATHON OIL CO must contact NDIC Field Inspector Ashleigh Devenberg at 701-290-3277 prior to
location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well drilling
and completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will prevent
pollution of the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits are
prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use. Drill
cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC. The
proposed directional plan is at a legal location. The minimum legal coordinate from the well head at casing point is:
625 N. Also, based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum legal coordinate from the well head is: 10803
N.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the
approved drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to
commence before the 3rd business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may be
waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information necessary to
evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other information that
would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the drilling permit, the
applicant should retain the permit.
William F Groffy
June 23, 2014
Page 2
Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card. It is requested that notification be given
immediately upon the spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the Oil & Gas Division, Bismarck,
via telephone. The following information must be included: Well name, legal location, permit number, drilling
contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding. Office hours are 8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m. and 1:00 p.m.
to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a message if after hours or on the weekend.
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor
shall file a certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys must
be submitted as one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director may require the
directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the operation of the
director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe document, with a
certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve (or
when sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Confidential status
Your request for confidential status of all information furnished to the Director, or his representatives, is hereby
granted. Such information, except production runs, shall remain confidential for six months commencing on the date
the well is spud.
Confidential status notwithstanding, the Director and his representatives shall have access to all well records
wherever located. Your company personnel, or any person performing work for your company shall permit the
Director and his representatives to come upon any lease, property, well, or drilling rig operated or controlled by them,
complying with all safety rules, and to inspect the records and operation of such wells and to have access at all times to
any and all records of wells. The Commission's field personnel periodically inspect producing and drilling wells. Any
information regarding such wells shall be made available to them at any time upon request. The information so
obtained by the field personnel shall be maintained in strict confidence and shall be available only to the Commission
and its staff.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12 hours,
and tail cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi before drilling the
plug or initiating tests.
Logs
NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well
bore, and (3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic
cement evaluation log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior
to completing the well. All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format)
copy and one digital LAS (log ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or
attached to an email sent to digitallogs@nd.gov Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
David Burns
Engineering Technician

NOTE: A Gamma Ray log must be run to ground surface and a CBL must be run on intermediate or longstring casing string if set.
Surveys are required at least every 30 feet in the build section and every 90 feet in the lateral section of a horizontal well. Measurement
inaccuracies are not considered when determining compliance with the spacing/drilling unit boundary setback requirement except in the
following scenarios: 1) When the angle between the well bore and the respective boundary is 10 degrees or less; or 2) If Industry standard
methods and equipment are not utilized. Consult the applicable field order for exceptions.
If measurement inaccuracies are required to be considered, a 2° MWD measurement inaccuracy will be applied to the horizontal portion of the well
bore. This measurement inaccuracy is applied to the well bore from KOP to TD.
REQUIRED ATTACHMENTS: Certified surveyor's plat, horizontal section plat, estimated geological tops, proposed mud/cementing plan,
directional plot/plan, $100 fee.

April 9, 2014
RE: Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director
Marathon Oil Company

1.
BOP EQUIPMENT
Marathon Oil Company's minimum specifications for pressure
control equipment are as follows:
Ram Type:
13 5/8" 5000 psi blind, pipe and annular.
a. Due to Marathon's experience it is felt that the above
referenced BOP equipment is adequate for drilling this well.
The reduced permeability of the target zone along with
Marathon's area experience of drilling over 250 horizontal
wells indicate that a MASP of 3000 psi is more adjusted to
the reality of the reservoir.
BOP and other equipment testing:
a. Floor valve, dart valve, kill valves, check valve, manual
choke line valve, manual top drive valve, hydraulic top
drive valve, HCR, choke house valves, choke manifold,
choke hose, choke line, kill line, upper pipe rams, lower
pipe rams, blind rams (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min. High
Test: 5000 psi x 10 min.)
b. Annular Preventer (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min. High Test:
2500 psi x 10 min.)
c. Rotating head and Orbit Valve (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min.
High Test: 1500 psi x 10 min.)
Frequency:
a. After initial installation (NU BOPE).
b. Whenever any seal subject to test pressure is broken.
c. After any repairs compromising seal.
d. At 30-day intervals.
All other equipment (upper and lower Kelly cocks, IBOP,
etc) will be tested according to Onshore Oil and Gas
Order No. 2.

ABNORMAL PRESSURES AND H2S GAS
a. The maximum anticipated bottom-hole pressure is 7810 psi.

6.
Well Completion
a. A 4 ½" liner will be run from above the 7" casing shoe to
the bottom of the well.
Liner has frac sleeves
installed.
b. Tie back liner will be run from top of 4 ½" Liner back to
the surface.
c. Well will be fractured utilizing a 30 stage frac.
d. Pursuant to NDIC letter effective February 12,2014,
concerning Hydraulic Fracture Stimulation using Diesel
Fuels, Marathon Oil Company will not inject diesel fuel
or any diesel-type chemicals (68334-30-5, 68476-34-6,
68476-30-2, 68476-31-3, or 8008-20-6) during the
hydraulic fracture stimulation process or this well.
Marathon understands the guidelines that are outline in
the above referenced letter including the requirement to
obtain an Underground Injection Control, Class II permit
from the NDIC prior to commencing any Hydraulic Fracture
Stimulation in which any amount of diesel fuel or any
diesel type chemical is injected.

Gas Capture Plan
Krebs 34-20TFH
Sec 29 T146N R93W
Field: Bailey
Flowback Strategy
Anticipated First Production date
The Krebs 34-20TFH is expected to commence production around February 2015. It is anticipated that it will be
connected to a gas sales pipeline at first production.
Multi-well startup
The well is expected to flowback concurrently with one of the other wells on the Krebs location. Flowback of the
well is expected to be approximately 4-10 days in duration.
Anticipated Oil and Gas Rates
Average Gas rate from the well during flowback is anticipated to be around 500 MSCFD.
Average Gas rate from the wellpad during flowback is anticipated to be around 1,900 MSCFD
Average Oil Rate from the well during flowback is anticipated to be around 700 bopd
Average Oil Rate from the wellpad during flowback is anticipated to be around 2,900 bopd
